==PAGE:151==
Appendix E
LWA Water absorption
Purpose
This method is based on DS/EN 1097-6:2013 which determines the absorption and den-
sity of lightweight aggregates. The tests were performed in collaboration with EØH.
Equipment
Pycnometers, 500 mL
Pycnometers, 100 mL
Thermometer
Procedure
The lightweight aggregates are dried over night before they can be used in the absorption
test.
The test portion is immersed in water in the pycnometer and entrapped air is
removed by gently rolling and jolting the pycnometer in a tipped position.
To keep
track of the temperature of the water in the pycnometer, it is placed, along side a
thermometer in a water bath with room temperature.
Every time a measurement is
needed the pycnometer is opened, overlled with water, closed again, and dried on the
outside before it is weighed. When all measurements are complete after 24 hours, the
aggregates are removed from the water and dried to a surface dried condition.

Appendix F
LWAC
This appendix includes all supplementary information regarding the LWAC blocks.
• Mixing procedure
• Mails regarding the mix and use of block machine
• Calculation of water content in LWAC blocks
• Final mixing ratios for all blocks
• Overview of all specimens
• Information regarding the hardening conditions
• Results from compressive strength tests
• Raw data concerning the water content at time of compressive strength test
• T-test raw data
• Results from capillary suction test
• Data sheets for LWA and a Leca block 600
==PAGE:160==
52
LWAC
F.1
Mixing LWAC blocks
The rst part of this appendix section explains the procedure of mixing lightweight con-
crete blocks in this project using the block machine from Abeo.
The procedure was
written in collaboration with EØH.
The overall procedure consists of
1. Drying the lightweight aggregates.
2. Mixing aggregates, cement, coal y ash and water.
3. Preparing and lling the mould.
4. Compressing and vibrating the mould.
5. Hardening process
6. Cutting cores or cubes
Drying the lightweight aggregates
Before using the aggregates in the mixture it is preferable to dry them, to make sure that
the water content is close to zero. This was done for at least 24 hours at 100◦C in the
big oven shown in Figure F.1a.
==PAGE:161==
Mixing LWAC blocks
53
(a)
Oven used to dry aggregates
(b)
Standard concrete mixer
Figure F.1
Mixing aggregates, cement, y ash and water
Materials are mixed in a standard concrete mixer, as shown in Figure F.1b. The mixing
is done in the following order.
1. Mix LWA 0-2 and the water corresponding the mixture of a reference sample.
2. Add LWA 2-4 and LWA 4-10
3. Wait for one hour to allow the aggregates to absorb some of the water. Make sure
to crush any clumps forming during the mixing. LWA 0-2 is very keen to form
lumps, sometimes up to the size of a st.
4. Add cement, coal y ash, and bio ash. Note zero time. It is preferable to mix
cement and ash before adding it to the concrete mixer.
5. If the recipe prescribes additional water because of the bio ash, add it now, be
cautious however as a right consistency is more important than it is to use all the
water.
6. Make sure that the consistency of the mixture makes it possible to form a snow-
ball. This proves that the water content is appropriate.
==PAGE:162==
54
LWAC
Preparing and lling the mould
For the best results, it is important that the block machine and the base plate, shown
in Figure F.2, are positioned appropriate, both relative to each other and relative to the
ground.
Figure F.2: Base plate (A), Block machine (B), Build-in weight (C) Removable lifting bars (D).
1. Make sure that the base plate is levelled in both directions. This is done using
shims made from ber board.
2. Clean the base plate thoroughly, lubricate it, and cover it in plastic. The sheet of
plastic should be big enough to wrap around the nished block.
3. Place the machine over the base plate. There should be a gap of
5 mm between
the two, and the machine should be levelled. Lubricate the inside of the machine
in oil.
4. When lifting the machine, as seen in gure F.3a, a forklift is used, which lifts the
two removable lifting bars (D). These are hold up by two pieces of timber. Both
the timber and the lifting bars should be removed before casting.
==PAGE:163==
Mixing LWAC blocks
55
5. Lift the arm of the machine, so no load is on the weight, and turn on the weight. If
the arm is not lifted, the weight will have a deviation corresponding to the weight
of the arm.
6. Plug in the machine.
7. Fill the mould with the LWAC mix. Do it gradually, and compress by hand, as
you go. Depending on how large a block is needed, it can be lled more or less.
However, if the block is too high, it is virtually impossible to remove it from the
machine without the top of the block breaking. The best results seem to come from
lling the cavity about 3 cm from the top, as seen in Figure F.3b.
8. The left-over mixture should be thrown out in the dry concrete container, not the
wet. The reason for this is that all of the wet concrete is left to harden into a block,
and then taken out using a crane. The LWA concrete is not strong enough, and
can cause the block to break.
(a)
Lifting block machine
(b)
Filling mould
Figure F.3
Once the machine has been lled to a desired level, it is time to compress and vibrate
the block into shape. This is easiest done by three people.
1. Move the pressure plate over the concrete mix and lover it down.
==PAGE:164==
56
LWAC
2. Add the extension rod, to extend the lever to its full length.
3. Place a bubble level on top of the pressure plate, and use a hammer to get it
levelled.
4. Turn on the vibration.
5. Gradually increase the pressure, while making sure that the pressure plate is lev-
elled, and that the lever is square to the machine.
6. At a pressure around 280-290 kg, the machine will start to tilt. At this point, extra
weight shall be placed on the other end of the machine, to keep it down, while the
pressure is increased to around 300 kg.
7. Once the pressure is 300 kg and the pressure plate is level and not moving, the
vibration can be turned o, and the pressure can be lifted.
8. Unplug the machine, replace the timber and the lifting bars and lift the machine
using a forklift, as slowly and vertically as possibly.
9. Wrap the block in the plastic sheet.
Hardening process
After a day (or two, depending on content of bio ash) the block is moved from the base
plate. The block has a tendency to stick to the plate. If the plastic sheet is of sucient
strength, it can be used to start the movement, without damaging the block. After this,
the block should be placed in a controlled climate, with temperature above 15 ◦C and a
relative humidity between 35 % and 65 %.
Cutting cylinders or cubes
For testing purposes, the blocks should be cut into cylinders or cubes. Cylinders are
the easiest, but if the block is very weak, it is dicult, and cubes might be advisable.
When cutting cubes, assistance from a technician is needed, as the saw that students are
permitted to use does not have sucient clearance for the block. When cutting cylinders,
the rst choice is what size to cut them to. The smaller the size, the more samples from
each casting, but the diameter should not be less than 70 mm according to DS/EN 1354-
2005. A block can yield seven cores if they are 100 mm each, and 12 if they are 75 mm.
The procedure is as follows:
1. Bring the core-drilling machine to a place where there are power, water and drain.
==PAGE:165==
Mixing LWAC blocks
57
2. Install the chosen drilling head. An adaptor might be needed.
3. Hook up power and water, and check that it is working.
4. Place a piece of wood underneath the drill, where the block will sit, to provide a
smooth base. This can help prevent chip out in the bottom of the core.
5. Place the block underneath the drill and start drilling cores. At rst, the weight of
the block is sucient to keep it in place, but as cores are drilled, and it gets lighter
it might be a good idea to clamp it down.
Once the cores are drilled, they should be shortened to the appropriate size using
the circular saw. DS/EN 1354-2005 prescribes that the height should be equal to the
diameter.
This means that most cores can become two specimens.
Make sure that
specimens have a sawn face on each side to provide the best results.

LWAC

Hej Randi og Esben.
 
Selv tak for sidst. Håber I kom godt hjem og der ikke gik hul på poserne undervejs.
 
Angående blokke, så tror jeg det nemmeste er, hvis jeg kommer forbi med dem selv. Jeg bor i Birkerød og så er Lyngby
næsten lige på vejen.
Har i vinterferie eller hvornår passer det jer, at jeg kan komme forbi? I morgen eller i starten  af næste uge? Nu er
Bygning 118 jo ikke helt lille, men jeg kan bare henvende mig i recep㯽ᔉonen eller hvad I kalder det lille glasbur I har
nede ved indgangen.

1.       Tilsæt 25 liter vand
2.       Tilsæt Leca® klinker (skal have 㯽ᔉd 㯽ᔉl at suge vandet)
3.       Tilsæt cement+ﬂyveaske
4.       Tilsæt 100 liter vand.

Hej Esben og Randi,
 
Så vidt jeg husker, trykkede vi med lidt mindre end 300 kg (270‐280 kg), fordi maskinen ellers vippede. Vi stoppede
med at presse, når vi kunne fornemme, at blokken ikke kunne presses mere sammen (hvilket var e薑╏er ca. 60 s).  
 
Beklager mit sene svar, men jeg har ikke tjekket mails på min ferie.
 
Hilsen Mia
 
Fra: Randi Juel Olsen [mailto:s092804@student.dtu.dk]

Hej Mia
Vi ved du er på ferie og måske uden internet, men vi tager chancen og håber på du ser denne mail
alligevel. 
Vi har brugt blokmaskinen nogle gange nu og er blevet godt tilfredse med konsistensen af vores
blanding. 
Kurt har informeret os om, at vi skal presse blokkene med 300 kg i 60 sek. Det er info han har fra
Pinars rapport, som vi jo ikke selv kan se, da den er fortrolig. For at lave et jævnt tryk på 300 kg har
vi lavet et lod der passer. Da vi forsøgte at lave en blok med dette lod var det alt for tungt og
resulterede i at maskinen vippede, så Esben måtte sætte sig på den anden side. 
Vi vil egentlig bare høre, om du er enig i at jeres blokke blev trykket med 300 kg i 60 sek?

F.6
Hardening conditions
This appendix section contains the data from a logger which has been placed in the room
with the LWAC blocks. The data includes the temperature, which should be above 15
◦C, and the relative humidity, which should be between 35 and 65 %RH. These gures
also appear in the thesis of EØH.

==PAGE:185==
Compressive strength Tests
77
F.7
Compressive strength Tests
This appendix section includes the data from the performed pressure tests. The samples
are sorted due to their age when tested and the following information is given for each
sample:
• Weight right before the pressure test is performed.
• Water content measured after the pressure test. The water content should not be
below 4 weight-% according to DS/EN 1354:2005. If that has been the case the
water content is written in red.
• Dry density calculated by the weight adjusted by the water content and the mea-
sured volume seen in appendix F.5.
• Pressure strength in kN and MPa, including average and standard deviation for
every block.
In section F.7.5 the T-test calculations are given as an output from excel.
If the
P-value is below 5 % it is written in red.

 og Kommissionens delegerede forordning (EU) No 574/2014.

2.
